      <p>The <b>House of Stuart</b>, originally <b>Stewart</b>, was a European <a href="/wiki/Dynasty" title="Dynasty">royal house</a> of Scotland with Breton origin.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">[2]</a></sup> They had held the office of <a href="/wiki/High_Steward_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="High Steward of Scotland">High Steward of Scotland</a> since <a href="/wiki/Walter_fitz_Alan" title="Walter fitz Alan">Walter fitz Alan</a> (c. 1150). The royal Stewart line was founded by <a href="/wiki/Robert_II_of_Scotland" title="Robert II of Scotland">Robert II</a> whose descendants were kings and queens of Scotland from 1371 until the union with England in 1707. <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a> was brought up in France where she adopted the French spelling of the name <i>Stuart</i>. </p>
      <p>In 1503, <a href="/wiki/James_IV" class="mw-redirect" title="James IV">James IV</a> married <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret Tudor</a>, thus linking the royal houses of Scotland and England. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_I_of_England" title="Elizabeth I of England">Elizabeth I of England</a> died without issue in 1603, and James IV's great grandson <a href="/wiki/James_VI_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="James VI of Scotland">James VI of Scotland</a> succeeded to the thrones of England and Ireland as James I in the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">Union of the Crowns</a>. The Stuarts were monarchs of the British Isles and its growing empire until the death of <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Queen Anne</a> in 1714, except for the period of the Commonwealth between 1649 and 1660.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[note 3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In total, nine Stewart/Stuart monarchs ruled Scotland alone from 1371 until 1603. The last ruler of Scotland alone was James VI, who became the first dual monarch of England and Scotland in 1603. Two Stuart queens ruled the isles following the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> in 1688: <a href="/wiki/Mary_II_of_England" title="Mary II of England">Mary II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Anne</a>. Both were the Protestant daughters of <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James VII and II</a> by his first wife <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hyde" title="Anne Hyde">Anne Hyde</a> and the great-grandchildren of James VI and I. Their father had converted to Catholicism and his new wife gave birth to a son in 1688, who was brought up a Roman Catholic and preceded his half-sisters; so James was deposed by Parliament in 1689, in favour of his daughters. But neither had any children who survived to adulthood, so the crown passed to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a> on the death of Queen Anne in 1714 under the terms of the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Settlement_1701" title="Act of Settlement 1701">Act of Settlement 1701</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Act_of_Security_1704" title="Act of Security 1704">Act of Security 1704</a>. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399"></a>
          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section 
           <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.
           <span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>.            <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">July 2012</span>)</i></small>
           <small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small>
          </div></td>
        </tr>
       </tbody>
      </table> 
      <p>The name <i>Stewart</i> derives from the political position of office similar to a governor, known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Steward_(office)" title="Steward (office)">steward</a></i>. It was originally adopted as the family surname by <a href="/wiki/Walter_Stewart,_3rd_High_Steward_of_Scotland" title="Walter Stewart, 3rd High Steward of Scotland">Walter Stewart, 3rd High Steward of Scotland</a>, who was the third member of the family to hold the position. Prior to this, family names were not used, but instead they had <a href="/wiki/Patronym" class="mw-redirect" title="Patronym">patronyms</a> defined through the father; for example the first two High Stewards were known as <i><a href="/wiki/Fitz" title="Fitz">Fitz</a></i>Alan and FitzWalter respectively. The gallicised spelling was first borne by <a href="/wiki/John_Stewart_of_Darnley" title="John Stewart of Darnley">John Stewart of Darnley</a> after his time in the French wars. During the 16th century, the French spelling <i>Stuart</i> was adopted by <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a>, when she was living in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">France</a>. She sanctioned the change to ensure the correct pronunciation of the <a href="/wiki/Scots_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Scots Language">Scots</a> version of the name <i>Stewart</i>, because retaining the letter "w" would have made it difficult for French speakers, who followed the Germans in usually rendering "w" as /v/. The spelling <i>Stuart</i> was also used by her second husband, <a href="/wiki/Henry_Stuart,_Lord_Darnley" title="Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley">Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley</a>; he was the father of <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a>, so the official spelling <i>Stuart</i> for the British royal family derives from him. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin:0 auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:858px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Stuart.png" class="image" title="Principal members of the house of Stuart following the 1603 Union of the Crowns."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6e/House_of_Stuart.png/850px-House_of_Stuart.png" decoding="async" width="850" height="364" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6e/House_of_Stuart.png/1275px-House_of_Stuart.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/6e/House_of_Stuart.png/1700px-House_of_Stuart.png 2x" data-file-width="2003" data-file-height="857"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:House_of_Stuart.png" title="File:House of Stuart.png"> </a>
         </div>Principal members of the house of Stuart following the 1603 Union of the Crowns.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The ancestral origins of the Stuart family are obscure—their probable ancestry is traced back to <a href="/wiki/Alan_FitzFlaad" class="mw-redirect" title="Alan FitzFlaad">Alan FitzFlaad</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Breton_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Breton people">Breton</a> who came over to Great Britain not long after the <a href="/wiki/Norman_conquest" class="mw-redirect" title="Norman conquest">Norman conquest</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stewartorigins_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stewartorigins-6">[3]</a></sup> Alan had been the hereditary steward of the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Dol" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Dol">Bishop</a> of <a href="/wiki/Dol-de-Bretagne" title="Dol-de-Bretagne">Dol</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brittany" title="Duchy of Brittany">Duchy of Brittany</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-bartlett_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bartlett-7">[4]</a></sup> Alan had a good relationship with <a href="/wiki/Henry_I_of_England" title="Henry I of England">Henry I of England</a> who awarded him with lands in <a href="/wiki/Shropshire" title="Shropshire">Shropshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bartlett_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bartlett-7">[4]</a></sup> The FitzAlan family quickly established themselves as a prominent <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Normans" title="Anglo-Normans">Anglo-Norman</a> noble house, with some of its members serving as <a href="/wiki/High_Sheriff_of_Shropshire" title="High Sheriff of Shropshire">High Sheriff of Shropshire</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bartlett_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bartlett-7">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[5]</a></sup> It was the great-grandson of Alan named <a href="/wiki/Walter_FitzAlan" class="mw-redirect" title="Walter FitzAlan">Walter FitzAlan</a> who became the first hereditary <a href="/wiki/High_Steward_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="High Steward of Scotland">High Steward of Scotland</a>, while his brother William's family went on to become <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Arundel" title="Earl of Arundel">Earls of Arundel</a>. </p>
      <p>When the civil war in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">Kingdom of England</a>, known as <a href="/wiki/The_Anarchy" title="The Anarchy">The Anarchy</a>, broke out between legitimist claimant <a href="/wiki/Empress_Matilda" title="Empress Matilda">Matilda, Lady of the English</a> and her cousin who had usurped her, <a href="/wiki/Stephen_of_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Stephen of England">King Stephen</a>, Walter had sided with Matilda.<sup id="cite_ref-king_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-9">[6]</a></sup> Another supporter of Matilda was her uncle <a href="/wiki/David_I_of_Scotland" title="David I of Scotland">David I of Scotland</a> from the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Dunkeld" title="House of Dunkeld">House of Dunkeld</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-king_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-9">[6]</a></sup> After Matilda was pushed out of England into the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Anjou" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Anjou">County of Anjou</a>, essentially failing in her legitimist attempt for the throne, many of her supporters in England fled also. It was then that Walter followed David up to the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Scotland" title="Kingdom of Scotland">Kingdom of Scotland</a>, where he was granted lands in <a href="/wiki/Renfrewshire" title="Renfrewshire">Renfrewshire</a> and the title for life of Lord High Steward.<sup id="cite_ref-king_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-king-9">[6]</a></sup> The next monarch of Scotland, <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_IV_of_Scotland" title="Malcolm IV of Scotland">Malcolm IV</a>, made the High Steward title a hereditary arrangement. While High Stewards, the family were based at <a href="/wiki/Dundonald,_South_Ayrshire" title="Dundonald, South Ayrshire">Dundonald, South Ayrshire</a> between the 12th and 13th centuries. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <p>The sixth High Steward of Scotland, <a href="/wiki/Walter_Stewart,_6th_High_Steward_of_Scotland" title="Walter Stewart, 6th High Steward of Scotland">Walter Stewart</a> (1293–1326), married <a href="/wiki/Marjorie_Bruce" title="Marjorie Bruce">Marjorie</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Robert_the_Bruce" title="Robert the Bruce">Robert the Bruce</a>, and also played an important part in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bannockburn" title="Battle of Bannockburn">Battle of Bannockburn</a> gaining further favour. Their son <a href="/wiki/Robert_II_of_Scotland" title="Robert II of Scotland">Robert</a> was heir to the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Bruce" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Bruce">House of Bruce</a>, the Lordship of Cunningham and the Bruce lands of <a href="/wiki/Bourtreehill" title="Bourtreehill">Bourtreehill</a>; he eventually inherited the Scottish throne when his uncle <a href="/wiki/David_II_of_Scotland" title="David II of Scotland">David II</a> died childless in 1371. </p>
      <p>In 1503, <a href="/wiki/James_IV_of_Scotland" title="James IV of Scotland">James IV</a> attempted to secure peace with <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_England" title="Kingdom of England">England</a> by marrying <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">King Henry VII</a>'s daughter, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Tudor" title="Margaret Tudor">Margaret Tudor</a>. The birth of their son, later <a href="/wiki/James_V_of_Scotland" title="James V of Scotland">James V</a>, brought the House of Stewart into the line of descent of the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Tudor" title="House of Tudor">House of Tudor</a>, and the English throne. Margaret Tudor later married <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Douglas,_6th_Earl_of_Angus" title="Archibald Douglas, 6th Earl of Angus">Archibald Douglas, 6th Earl of Angus</a>, and their daughter, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Douglas" title="Margaret Douglas">Margaret Douglas</a>, was the mother of <a href="/wiki/Henry_Stuart,_Lord_Darnley" title="Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley">Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley</a>. In 1565, Darnley married his half-cousin <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/James_V_of_Scotland" title="James V of Scotland">James V</a>. Darnley's father was <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Stewart,_4th_Earl_of_Lennox" title="Matthew Stewart, 4th Earl of Lennox">Matthew Stewart, 4th Earl of Lennox</a>, a member of the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_of_Darnley" title="Stewart of Darnley">Stewart of Darnley</a> branch of the House. Lennox was a descendant of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Stewart,_4th_High_Steward_of_Scotland" title="Alexander Stewart, 4th High Steward of Scotland">Alexander Stewart, 4th High Steward of Scotland</a>, also descended from <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_Scotland" title="James II of Scotland">James II</a>, being Mary's <a href="/wiki/Heir_presumptive" title="Heir presumptive">heir presumptive</a>. Thus Darnley was also related to Mary on his father's side and because of this connection, Mary's heirs remained part of the House of Stuart. Following <a href="/wiki/John_Stewart_of_Darnley" title="John Stewart of Darnley">John Stewart of Darnley</a>'s ennoblement for his part at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Baug%C3%A9" title="Battle of Baugé">Battle of Baugé</a> in 1421 and the grant of lands to him at <a href="/wiki/Aubigny-sur-N%C3%A8re" title="Aubigny-sur-Nère">Aubigny</a> and <a href="/wiki/Concressault" title="Concressault">Concressault</a>, the Darnley Stewarts' surname was gallicised to <i>Stuart</i>. </p>
      <p>Both Mary, Queen of Scots, and Lord Darnley had strong claims on the English throne, through their mutual grandmother, Margaret Tudor. This eventually led to the accession of the couple's only child <a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James</a> as King of Scotland, England, and Ireland in 1603. However, this was a <a href="/wiki/Personal_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Personal Union">Personal Union</a>, as the three Kingdoms shared a monarch, but had separate governments, churches, and institutions. Indeed, the personal union did not prevent an armed conflict, known as the <a href="/wiki/Bishops%27_Wars" title="Bishops' Wars">Bishops' Wars</a>, breaking out between England and Scotland in 1639. This was to become part of the cycle of political and military conflict that marked the reign of <a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a>, Scotland and Ireland, culminating in a series of conflicts known as the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Three_Kingdoms" class="mw-redirect" title="War of the Three Kingdoms">War of the Three Kingdoms</a>. The trial and execution of Charles I by the English Parliament in 1649 began 11 years of republican government known as the <a href="/wiki/English_Interregnum" class="mw-redirect" title="English Interregnum">English Interregnum</a>. Scotland initially recognised the late King's son, also called <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles</a>, as their monarch, before being subjugated and forced to enter Cromwell's Commonwealth by <a href="/wiki/George_Monck,_1st_Duke_of_Albemarle" title="George Monck, 1st Duke of Albemarle">General Monck</a>'s occupying army. During this period, the principal members of the House of Stuart lived in exile in <a href="/wiki/Mainland_Europe" class="mw-redirect" title="Mainland Europe">mainland Europe</a>. The younger Charles returned to Britain to assume his three thrones in 1660 as "<a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a>, Scotland and Ireland", but dated his reign from his father's death eleven years before. </p>
      <p>In feudal and dynastic terms, the Scottish reliance on French support was revived during the reign of <a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a>, whose own mother was French. His sister <a href="/wiki/Henrietta_Anne_Stuart" class="mw-redirect" title="Henrietta Anne Stuart">Henrietta</a> married into the French royal family. Charles II left no legitimate children, but his numerous illegitimate descendants included the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Buccleuch" title="Duke of Buccleuch">Dukes of Buccleuch</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Grafton" title="Duke of Grafton">Dukes of Grafton</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Saint_Albans" class="mw-redirect" title="Duke of Saint Albans">Dukes of Saint Albans</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Richmond" title="Duke of Richmond">Dukes of Richmond</a>. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_(1).JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG/290px-0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG" decoding="async" width="290" height="193" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG/435px-0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c8/0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG/580px-0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_%281%29.JPG 2x" data-file-width="7087" data-file-height="4724"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:0_Monument_fun%C3%A9raire_des_derniers_Stuarts_-_Basilique_St-Pierre_-_Vatican_(1).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Monument_to_the_Royal_Stuarts" title="Monument to the Royal Stuarts">Monument to the Royal Stuarts</a> in 
         <a href="/wiki/St._Peter%27s_Basilica" title="St. Peter's Basilica">St. Peter's Basilica</a> – Work of 
         <a href="/wiki/Antonio_Canova" title="Antonio Canova">Antonio Canova</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>These French and Roman Catholic connections proved unpopular and resulted in the downfall of the Stuarts, whose mutual enemies identified with Protestantism and because <a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James VII and II</a> offended the Anglican establishment by proposing tolerance not only for Catholics but for Protestant Dissenters. The <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Glorious Revolution</a> caused the overthrow of King James in favour of his son-in-law and his daughter, <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mary_II_of_England" title="Mary II of England">Mary</a>. James continued to claim the thrones of England and Scotland to which he had been crowned, and encouraged <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_risings" title="Jacobite risings">revolts</a> in his name, and his grandson <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles</a> (also known as Bonnie Prince Charlie) led an ultimately <a href="/wiki/Jacobite_rising_of_1745" title="Jacobite rising of 1745">unsuccessful rising in 1745</a>, ironically becoming symbols of conservative <a href="/wiki/Radicalism_(historical)" title="Radicalism (historical)">rebellion</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romanticism</a>. Some blame the identification of the Roman Catholic Church with the Stuarts for the extremely lengthy delay in the passage of <a href="/wiki/Catholic_emancipation" title="Catholic emancipation">Catholic emancipation</a> until Jacobitism (as represented by direct Stuart heirs) was extinguished; however it was as likely to be caused by entrenched anti-Catholic prejudice among the Anglican establishment of England. Despite the <a href="/wiki/British_Whig_Party" class="mw-redirect" title="British Whig Party">Whig</a> intentions of tolerance to be extended to <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Ireland" title="Kingdom of Ireland">Irish subjects</a>, this was not the preference of Georgian Tories and their failure at compromise played a subsequent role in the present division of Ireland.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Present-day">Present-day</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Present-day">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The Royal House of Stuart became extinct with the death of Cardinal <a href="/wiki/Henry_Benedict_Stuart" title="Henry Benedict Stuart">Henry Benedict Stuart</a>, brother of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Edward_Stuart" title="Charles Edward Stuart">Charles Edward Stuart</a>, in 1807. <a href="/wiki/Franz,_Duke_of_Bavaria" title="Franz, Duke of Bavaria">Duke Francis of Bavaria</a> is the current senior heir.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">[7]</a></sup> However, Charles II had a number of illegitimate sons whose surviving <a href="/wiki/Descendants_of_Charles_II_of_England" title="Descendants of Charles II of England">descendants in the male line</a> include <a href="/wiki/Charles_Gordon-Lennox,_11th_Duke_of_Richmond" title="Charles Gordon-Lennox, 11th Duke of Richmond">Charles Gordon-Lennox, 11th Duke of Richmond</a>; <a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_12th_Duke_of_Grafton" title="Henry FitzRoy, 12th Duke of Grafton">Henry FitzRoy, 12th Duke of Grafton</a>; <a href="/wiki/Murray_Beauclerk,_14th_Duke_of_St_Albans" title="Murray Beauclerk, 14th Duke of St Albans">Murray Beauclerk, 14th Duke of St Albans</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Richard_Scott,_10th_Duke_of_Buccleuch" title="Richard Scott, 10th Duke of Buccleuch">Richard Scott, 10th Duke of Buccleuch</a>. In addition, James II's illegitimate son, <a href="/wiki/James_FitzJames,_1st_Duke_of_Berwick" title="James FitzJames, 1st Duke of Berwick">James FitzJames, 1st Duke of Berwick</a>, founded the <a href="/wiki/House_of_FitzJames" title="House of FitzJames">House of FitzJames</a> comprising two branches, one in France and one in Spain. The last of the French branch died in 1967; the senior heir of James II's male line descendants is <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jacobo_Hernando_Fitz-James_Stuart,_16th_Duke_of_Pe%C3%B1aranda_de_Duero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jacobo Hernando Fitz-James Stuart, 16th Duke of Peñaranda de Duero (page does not exist)">Jacobo Hernando Fitz-James Stuart, 16th Duke of Peñaranda de Duero</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_monarchs">List of monarchs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: List of monarchs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h3><span id="Monarchs_of_England.2C_Scotland_and_Ireland"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Monarchs_of_England,_Scotland_and_Ireland">Monarchs of England, Scotland and Ireland</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Monarchs of England, Scotland and Ireland">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tbody>
        <tr>
         <td class="mbox-image">
          <div style="width:52px">

          </div></td>
         <td class="mbox-text">
          <div class="mbox-text-span">
           This section

      <p>From the <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a>, which came into effect on 1 May 1707, the last Stuart monarch, Anne, became Queen of Great Britain and Ireland. </p>

        </tr>

         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_(James_VI_of_Scotland)_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Paul van Somer - James I of England (James VI of Scotland) - Google Art Project.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/80px-Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="80" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/120px-Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/159px-Paul_van_Somer_-_James_I_of_England_%28James_VI_of_Scotland%29_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4196" data-file-height="6676"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a> <br></td> 
         <td>24 March 1603</td> 
         <td align="center">27 March 1625</td> 
         <td>Great-Great grandson of <a href="/wiki/Henry_VII_of_England" title="Henry VII of England">Henry VII of England</a>. King of Scotland alone until inheriting the titles King of England and Ireland, including claim to France from the extinct <a href="/wiki/House_of_Tudor" title="House of Tudor">Tudors</a>. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I,_King_of_England_(Copy)_-_WGA07384.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Anthony van Dyck - Equestrian Portrait of Charles I, King of England (Copy) - WGA07384.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg/79px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg" decoding="async" width="79" height="114" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg/119px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg/159px-Anthony_van_Dyck_-_Equestrian_Portrait_of_Charles_I%2C_King_of_England_%28Copy%29_-_WGA07384.jpg 2x" data-file-width="637" data-file-height="914"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I</a></td> 
         <td align="center">27 March 1625</td> 
         <td align="center">30 January 1649 (executed)</td> 
         <td>son of James VI and I </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Charles II of England by Kneller.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg/79px-Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg" decoding="async" width="79" height="131" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg/120px-Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg/159px-Charles_II_of_England_by_Kneller.jpg 2x" data-file-width="810" data-file-height="1333"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II</a></td> 
         <td align="center">30 January 1649 (de jure); 2 May 1660 (de facto)</td> 
         <td align="center">6 February 1685</td> 
         <td>son of Charles I. Prohibited by Parliament from assuming the throne during a republican period of government known as the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_England" title="Commonwealth of England">Commonwealth of England</a>, but then accepted as king in 1661. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II,_when_Duke_of_York,_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Sir Peter Lely - James VII and II, when Duke of York, 1633 – 1701 - Google Art Project.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/79px-Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" decoding="async" width="79" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/119px-Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/159px-Sir_Peter_Lely_-_James_VII_and_II%2C_when_Duke_of_York%2C_1633_%E2%80%93_1701_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3182" data-file-height="4001"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/James_II_of_England" title="James II of England">James VII and II</a></td> 
         <td align="center">6 February 1685</td> 
         <td align="center">11 December 1688</td> 
         <td>brother of Charles II, who died without legitimate issue. Son of Charles I. Overthrown at the <a href="/wiki/Glorious_Revolution" title="Glorious Revolution">Revolution of 1688</a>. Died in 1701. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Mary_II.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Queen Mary II.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Queen_Mary_II.jpg/80px-Queen_Mary_II.jpg" decoding="async" width="80" height="97" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Queen_Mary_II.jpg/120px-Queen_Mary_II.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Queen_Mary_II.jpg/160px-Queen_Mary_II.jpg 2x" data-file-width="746" data-file-height="900"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Mary_II_of_England" title="Mary II of England">Mary II</a></td> 
         <td align="center">13 February 1689</td> 
         <td align="center">28 December 1694</td> 
         <td>daughter of James II &amp; VII, who was still alive and pretending to the throne. Co-monarch was <a href="/wiki/William_III_of_England" title="William III of England">William III &amp; II</a> who outlived his wife. </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/File:Wissing,_Willem_-_Queen_Anne,_1687.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Wissing, Willem - Queen Anne, 1687.jpg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg/80px-Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg" decoding="async" width="80" height="99" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg/120px-Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg/160px-Wissing%2C_Willem_-_Queen_Anne%2C_1687.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1287" data-file-height="1600"></a></td> 
         <td align="center"><a href="/wiki/Anne,_Queen_of_Great_Britain" title="Anne, Queen of Great Britain">Anne</a></td> 
         <td align="center">8 March 1702</td> 
         <td align="center">1 August 1714</td> 
         <td>sister of Mary II. daughter of James II &amp; VII. Name of state changed to Great Britain with the political <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Union_1707" title="Acts of Union 1707">Acts of Union 1707</a>, though family has used title since James I &amp; VI. Died childless, rights pass to <a href="/wiki/House_of_Hanover" title="House of Hanover">House of Hanover</a>. </td>
        </tr>

       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Family_tree">Family tree</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Family tree">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
        See also: 
        <a href="/wiki/Scottish_monarchs%27_family_tree#House_of_Stewart" class="mw-redirect" title="Scottish monarchs' family tree">Stuart Scottish monarchs family tree</a> and

       <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="House_of_Stuart">House of Stuart</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: House of Stuart">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
       <p>Descended from the <a href="/wiki/Stewart_of_Darnley" title="Stewart of Darnley">Stewarts of Darnley</a> (Stewarts of Lennox) </p> 
       <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r886050385">
       <div class="treeview"> 
        <ul>
         <li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Stuart,_Lord_Darnley" title="Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley">Henry Stuart, Lord Darnley</a>, husband of <a href="/wiki/Mary,_Queen_of_Scots" title="Mary, Queen of Scots">Mary, Queen of Scots</a> 
          <ul>
           <li><a href="/wiki/James_VI_and_I" title="James VI and I">James VI and I</a> 
            <ul>
             <li><a href="/wiki/Henry_Frederick,_Prince_of_Wales" title="Henry Frederick, Prince of Wales">Henry Frederick, Prince of Wales</a></li> 
             <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_I_of_England" title="Charles I of England">Charles I of England</a> 
              <ul>
               <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_II_of_England" title="Charles II of England">Charles II of England</a> 
                <ul>
                 <li><a href="/wiki/James_Scott,_1st_Duke_of_Monmouth" title="James Scott, 1st Duke of Monmouth">James Scott, 1st Duke of Monmouth</a> (illegitimate) 
                  <ul>
                   <li><i><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Buccleuch" title="Duke of Buccleuch">Dukes of Buccleuch</a></i></li>
                  </ul></li> 
                 <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_FitzCharles,_1st_Earl_of_Plymouth" title="Charles FitzCharles, 1st Earl of Plymouth">Charles FitzCharles, 1st Earl of Plymouth</a> (illegitimate)</li> 
                 <li><a href="/wiki/Charles_FitzRoy,_2nd_Duke_of_Cleveland" title="Charles FitzRoy, 2nd Duke of Cleveland">Charles FitzRoy, 2nd Duke of Cleveland</a> (illegitimate) 
                  <ul>
                   <li><i><a href="/wiki/Duke_of_Cleveland" title="Duke of Cleveland">Dukes of Cleveland</a></i> (extinct 1774)</li>
                  </ul></li> 
                 <li><a href="/wiki/Henry_FitzRoy,_1st_Duke_of_Grafton" title="Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Grafton">Henry FitzRoy, 1st Duke of Grafton</a> (illegitimate)

       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

       <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=House_of_Stuart&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
       <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;"> 
        <div class="mw-references-wrap">
         <ol class="references"> 
          <li id="cite_note-France-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-France_1-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">titular claim rather than <i>de facto</i></span> </li> 
          <li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The progenitor of the Stuarts was <a href="/wiki/Walter_fitz_Alan" title="Walter fitz Alan">Walter fitz Alan</a>, a Breton.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">[1]</a></sup></span> </li> 
          <li id="cite_note-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-5">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Earl_of_Galloway" title="Earl of Galloway">Earls of Galloway</a> are the senior surviving line of the Stuarts. They are descended from a line which originated from the second son of <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Stewart,_4th_High_Steward_of_Scotland" title="Alexander Stewart, 4th High Steward of Scotland">Alexander Stewart, 4th High Steward of Scotland</a> and are not members of the Stewart/Stuart royal line; however, they are part of the peerage.</span> </li> 
         </ol>
        </div>
       </div>

           <div>
            <b> House of Stuart </b>
           </div> </td>
